LogName=Security
SourceName=Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4688
EventType=0
Type=Information
ComputerName=$SPLUNK_HOME/etc/apps/Splunk_TA_windows/samples/hostname.sample
TaskCategory=Process Creation
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=120502497
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=A new process has been created.
Subject:
	Security ID:		Domain_B\user_e
	Account Name:		user_e
	Account Domain:		Domain_B
	Logon ID:		0x0452
Process Information:
	New Process ID:		0x418C
	New Process Name:	C:\Windows\System32\example_g.exe
	Token Elevation Type:	TokenElevationTypeLimited (3)
	Creator Process ID:	0x8ABB
Token Elevation Type indicates the type of token that was assigned to the new process in accordance with User Account Control policy.
Type 1 is a full token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  A full token is only used if User Account Control is disabled or if the User is the built-in Administrator account or a service account.
Type 2 is an elevated token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  An elevated token is used when User Account Control is enabled and the User chooses to start the program using Run as administrator.  An elevated token is also used when an application is configured to always require administrative privilege or to always require maximum privilege, and the User is a member of the Administrators group.
Type 3 is a limited token with administrative privileges removed and administrative groups disabled.  The limited token is used when User Account Control is enabled, the application does not require administrative privilege, and the User does not choose to start the program using Run as administrator.

LogName=Security
SourceName= Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4624
EventType=0
Type=Information
ComputerName=PROD-POS-002
TaskCategory=Logon
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=999043306
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=An account was successfully logged on.

Subject:
 Security ID:  Domain_B\SYSTEM
 Account Name:  PROD-POS-002
 Account Domain:  Domain_B
 Logon ID:  0x70E4

Logon Information:
 Logon Type:  2
 Restricted Admin Mode: Yes
 Virtual Account:  No
 Elevated Token:  Yes

Impersonation Level:  Delegation

New Logon:
 Security ID:  Domain_B\user_d
 Account Name:  user_d
 Account Domain:  Domain_B
 Logon ID:  0x3EC3
 Linked Logon ID:  0A7C
 Network Account Name: -
 Network Account Domain: Domain_A
 Logon GUID:  {221B21A6-1AE2-3F9A-24EF-22C392AC2A47}

Process Information:
 Process ID:  0xF83C
 Process Name:  C:\Windows\System32\example_f.exe

Network Information:
 Workstation Name: PROD-POS-002
 Source Network Address: 237.42.135.113
 Source Port:  56848

Detailed Authentication Information:
 Logon Process:  User32 
 Authentication Package: Negotiate
 Transited Services: -
 Package Name (NTLM only): -
 Key Length:  0

This event is generated when a logon session is created. It is generated on the computer that was accessed.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as 1635E.exe or 1635E.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

LogName=Security
SourceName= Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4624
EventType=0
Type=Information
ComputerName=ops-sys-005
TaskCategory=Logon
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=299425023
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=An account was successfully logged on.

Subject:
 Security ID:  Domain_B\SYSTEM
 Account Name:  ops-sys-005
 Account Domain:  Domain_B
 Logon ID:  0x70E4

Logon Information:
 Logon Type:  7
 Restricted Admin Mode: Yes
 Virtual Account:  Yes
 Elevated Token:  No

Impersonation Level:  Impersonation

New Logon:
 Security ID:  Domain_B\user_f
 Account Name:  user_f
 Account Domain:  Domain_B
 Logon ID:  0xA369
 Linked Logon ID:  AFFA
 Network Account Name: -
 Network Account Domain: Domain_E
 Logon GUID:  {0887F1E4-39EA-D53C-804F-31D568A06274}

Process Information:
 Process ID:  0x47CC
 Process Name:  C:\Windows\System32\example_f.exe

Network Information:
 Workstation Name: ops-sys-005
 Source Network Address: 88.135.106.46
 Source Port:  18660

Detailed Authentication Information:
 Logon Process:  logonProcess1 
 Authentication Package: Negotiate
 Transited Services: service_D
 Package Name (NTLM only): -
 Key Length:  0

This event is generated when a logon session is created. It is generated on the computer that was accessed.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as 943D3.exe or 943D3.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

LogName=Security
SourceName=Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4688
EventType=0
Type=Information
ComputerName=$SPLUNK_HOME/etc/apps/Splunk_TA_windows/samples/hostname.sample
TaskCategory=Process Creation
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=403580115
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=A new process has been created.
Subject:
	Security ID:		Domain_D\user_l
	Account Name:		user_l
	Account Domain:		Domain_D
	Logon ID:		0xAB37
Process Information:
	New Process ID:		0x1483
	New Process Name:	C:\Windows\System32\example_a.exe
	Token Elevation Type:	TokenElevationTypeDefault (1)
	Creator Process ID:	0x8DE3
Token Elevation Type indicates the type of token that was assigned to the new process in accordance with User Account Control policy.
Type 1 is a full token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  A full token is only used if User Account Control is disabled or if the User is the built-in Administrator account or a service account.
Type 2 is an elevated token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  An elevated token is used when User Account Control is enabled and the User chooses to start the program using Run as administrator.  An elevated token is also used when an application is configured to always require administrative privilege or to always require maximum privilege, and the User is a member of the Administrators group.
Type 3 is a limited token with administrative privileges removed and administrative groups disabled.  The limited token is used when User Account Control is enabled, the application does not require administrative privilege, and the User does not choose to start the program using Run as administrator.

SourceName= Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4624
EventType=0
Type=Information
ComputerName=ACME-005
TaskCategory=Logon
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=842192265
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=An account was successfully logged on.

Subject:
 Security ID:  Domain_C\SYSTEM
 Account Name:  ACME-005
 Account Domain:  Domain_C
 Logon ID:  0x70E4

Logon Information:
 Logon Type:  11
 Restricted Admin Mode: Yes
 Virtual Account:  No
 Elevated Token:  Yes

Impersonation Level:  Impersonation

New Logon:
 Security ID:  Domain_C\user_b
 Account Name:  user_b
 Account Domain:  Domain_C
 Logon ID:  0x3A81
 Linked Logon ID:  A289
 Network Account Name: -
 Network Account Domain: Domain_E
 Logon GUID:  {27C4A2F2-13CA-AA25-E903-D31268740239}

Process Information:
 Process ID:  0xF1A9
 Process Name:  C:\Windows\System32\example_d.exe

Network Information:
 Workstation Name: ACME-005
 Source Network Address: -
 Source Port:  30922

Detailed Authentication Information:
 Logon Process:  logonProcess1 
 Authentication Package: Kerberos
 Transited Services: -
 Package Name (NTLM only): -
 Key Length:  0

This event is generated when a logon session is created. It is generated on the computer that was accessed.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as 92582.exe or 92582.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

LogName=Security
SourceName=Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4688
EventType=0
Type=Information
ComputerName=$SPLUNK_HOME/etc/apps/Splunk_TA_windows/samples/hostname.sample
TaskCategory=Process Creation
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=85778525
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=A new process has been created.
Subject:
	Security ID:		Domain_A\user_g
	Account Name:		user_g
	Account Domain:		Domain_A
	Logon ID:		0xEB5F
Process Information:
	New Process ID:		0xFA9C
	New Process Name:	C:\Windows\System32\example_b.exe
	Token Elevation Type:	TokenElevationTypeFull (2)
	Creator Process ID:	0x3D92
Token Elevation Type indicates the type of token that was assigned to the new process in accordance with User Account Control policy.
Type 1 is a full token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  A full token is only used if User Account Control is disabled or if the User is the built-in Administrator account or a service account.
Type 2 is an elevated token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  An elevated token is used when User Account Control is enabled and the User chooses to start the program using Run as administrator.  An elevated token is also used when an application is configured to always require administrative privilege or to always require maximum privilege, and the User is a member of the Administrators group.
Type 3 is a limited token with administrative privileges removed and administrative groups disabled.  The limited token is used when User Account Control is enabled, the application does not require administrative privilege, and the User does not choose to start the program using Run as administrator.

01/28/2020 01:21:22 PM
LogName=Security
SourceName= Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4624
EventType=0
Type=Information
ComputerName=SE-006
TaskCategory=Logon
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=376738958
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=An account was successfully logged on.

Subject:
 Security ID:  Domain_C\SYSTEM
 Account Name:  SE-006
 Account Domain:  Domain_C
 Logon ID:  0x70E4

Logon Information:
 Logon Type:  8
 Restricted Admin Mode: No
 Virtual Account:  Yes
 Elevated Token:  Yes

Impersonation Level:  Delegation

New Logon:
 Security ID:  Domain_C\user_m
 Account Name:  user_m
 Account Domain:  Domain_C
 Logon ID:  0x46BA
 Linked Logon ID:  DA5D
 Network Account Name: -
 Network Account Domain: Domain_A
 Logon GUID:  {0887F1E4-39EA-D53C-804F-31D568A06274}

Process Information:
 Process ID:  0xED36
 Process Name:  C:\Windows\System32\example_f.exe

Network Information:
 Workstation Name: SE-006
 Source Network Address: 119.213.134.113
 Source Port:  21194

Detailed Authentication Information:
 Logon Process:  logonProcess1 
 Authentication Package: Negotiate
 Transited Services: service_B
 Package Name (NTLM only): -
 Key Length:  0

This event is generated when a logon session is created. It is generated on the computer that was accessed.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as 5830E.exe or 5830E.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

LogName=Security
SourceName=Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4688
EventType=0
Type=Information
ComputerName=$SPLUNK_HOME/etc/apps/Splunk_TA_windows/samples/hostname.sample
TaskCategory=Process Creation
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=544848027
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=A new process has been created.
Subject:
	Security ID:		Domain_B\user_m
	Account Name:		user_m
	Account Domain:		Domain_B
	Logon ID:		0x46BA
Process Information:
	New Process ID:		0x4F89
	New Process Name:	C:\Windows\System32\example_d.exe
	Token Elevation Type:	TokenElevationTypeFull (2)
	Creator Process ID:	0xCAA0
Token Elevation Type indicates the type of token that was assigned to the new process in accordance with User Account Control policy.
Type 1 is a full token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  A full token is only used if User Account Control is disabled or if the User is the built-in Administrator account or a service account.
Type 2 is an elevated token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  An elevated token is used when User Account Control is enabled and the User chooses to start the program using Run as administrator.  An elevated token is also used when an application is configured to always require administrative privilege or to always require maximum privilege, and the User is a member of the Administrators group.
Type 3 is a limited token with administrative privileges removed and administrative groups disabled.  The limited token is used when User Account Control is enabled, the application does not require administrative privilege, and the User does not choose to start the program using Run as administrator.

LogName=Security
SourceName= Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4624
EventType=0
Type=Information
ComputerName=ACME-006
TaskCategory=Logon

RecordNumber=99981091
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=An account was successfully logged on.

Subject:
 Security ID:  Domain_C\SYSTEM
 Account Name:  ACME-006
 Account Domain:  Domain_C
 Logon ID:  0x70E4

Logon Information:
 Logon Type:  4
 Restricted Admin Mode: No
 Virtual Account:  Yes
 Elevated Token:  Yes

Impersonation Level:  Delegation

New Logon:
 Security ID:  Domain_C\user_c
 Account Name:  user_c
 Account Domain:  Domain_C
 Logon ID:  0x5FC9
 Linked Logon ID:  9DC8
 Network Account Name: user_e
 Network Account Domain: -
 Logon GUID:  {221B21A6-1AE2-3F9A-24EF-22C392AC2A47}

Process Information:
 Process ID:  0x6AEE
 Process Name:  C:\Windows\System32\example_a.exe

Network Information:
 Workstation Name: ACME-006
 Source Network Address: 195.236.159.204
 Source Port:  65075

Detailed Authentication Information:
 Logon Process:  logonProcess1 
 Authentication Package: Kerberos
 Transited Services: service_A
 Package Name (NTLM only): -
 Key Length:  0

This event is generated when a logon session is created. It is generated on the computer that was accessed.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as FB40E.exe or FB40E.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

LogName=Security
SourceName=Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4688
EventType=0
Type=Information
ComputerName=$SPLUNK_HOME/etc/apps/Splunk_TA_windows/samples/hostname.sample
TaskCategory=Process Creation
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=568682043
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=A new process has been created.
Subject:
	Security ID:		Domain_E\user_n
	Account Name:		user_n
	Account Domain:		Domain_E
	Logon ID:		0x4D76
Process Information:
	New Process ID:		0xADE2
	New Process Name:	C:\Windows\System32\example_a.exe
	Token Elevation Type:	TokenElevationTypeDefault (1)
	Creator Process ID:	0xA15F
Token Elevation Type indicates the type of token that was assigned to the new process in accordance with User Account Control policy.
Type 1 is a full token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  A full token is only used if User Account Control is disabled or if the User is the built-in Administrator account or a service account.
Type 2 is an elevated token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  An elevated token is used when User Account Control is enabled and the User chooses to start the program using Run as administrator.  An elevated token is also used when an application is configured to always require administrative privilege or to always require maximum privilege, and the User is a member of the Administrators group.
Type 3 is a limited token with administrative privileges removed and administrative groups disabled.  The limited token is used when User Account Control is enabled, the application does not require administrative privilege, and the User does not choose to start the program using Run as administrator.

TaskCategory=Process Creation
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=267957227
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=A new process has been created.
Subject:
	Security ID:		Domain_C\user_d
	Account Name:		user_d
	Account Domain:		Domain_C
	Logon ID:		0x3EC3
Process Information:
	New Process ID:		0xCEDC
	New Process Name:	C:\Windows\System32\example_e.exe
	Token Elevation Type:	TokenElevationTypeLimited (3)
	Creator Process ID:	0xE6F3
Token Elevation Type indicates the type of token that was assigned to the new process in accordance with User Account Control policy.
Type 1 is a full token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  A full token is only used if User Account Control is disabled or if the User is the built-in Administrator account or a service account.
Type 2 is an elevated token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  An elevated token is used when User Account Control is enabled and the User chooses to start the program using Run as administrator.  An elevated token is also used when an application is configured to always require administrative privilege or to always require maximum privilege, and the User is a member of the Administrators group.
Type 3 is a limited token with administrative privileges removed and administrative groups disabled.  The limited token is used when User Account Control is enabled, the application does not require administrative privilege, and the User does not choose to start the program using Run as administrator.

LogName=Security
SourceName= Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4624
EventType=0
Type=Information
ComputerName=ACME-006
TaskCategory=Logon
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=331685467
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=An account was successfully logged on.

Subject:
 Security ID:  Domain_E\SYSTEM
 Account Name:  ACME-006
 Account Domain:  Domain_E
 Logon ID:  0x70E4

Logon Information:
 Logon Type:  11
 Restricted Admin Mode: -
 Virtual Account:  No
 Elevated Token:  Yes

Impersonation Level:  Impersonation

New Logon:
 Security ID:  Domain_E\user_i
 Account Name:  user_i
 Account Domain:  Domain_E
 Logon ID:  0x5F25
 Linked Logon ID:  1DB4
 Network Account Name: user_j
 Network Account Domain: Domain_A
 Logon GUID:  {27C4A2F2-13CA-AA25-E903-D31268740239}

Process Information:
 Process ID:  0x155F
 Process Name:  C:\Windows\System32\example_c.exe

Network Information:
 Workstation Name: ACME-006
 Source Network Address: -
 Source Port:  18286

Detailed Authentication Information:
 Logon Process:  Winlogon 
 Authentication Package: Negotiate
 Transited Services: -
 Package Name (NTLM only): -
 Key Length:  0

This event is generated when a logon session is created. It is generated on the computer that was accessed.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as DAD63.exe or DAD63.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

01/28/2020 01:20:56 PM
LogName=Security
SourceName=Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4688
EventType=0
Type=Information
ComputerName=$SPLUNK_HOME/etc/apps/Splunk_TA_windows/samples/hostname.sample
TaskCategory=Process Creation
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=503447417
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=A new process has been created.
Subject:
	Security ID:		Domain_A\user_a
	Account Name:		user_a
	Account Domain:		Domain_A
	Logon ID:		0x6C10
Process Information:
	New Process ID:		0x710E
	New Process Name:	C:\Windows\System32\example_f.exe
	Token Elevation Type:	TokenElevationTypeFull (2)
	Creator Process ID:	0xA40B
Token Elevation Type indicates the type of token that was assigned to the new process in accordance with User Account Control policy.
Type 1 is a full token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  A full token is only used if User Account Control is disabled or if the User is the built-in Administrator account or a service account.
Type 2 is an elevated token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  An elevated token is used when User Account Control is enabled and the User chooses to start the program using Run as administrator.  An elevated token is also used when an application is configured to always require administrative privilege or to always require maximum privilege, and the User is a member of the Administrators group.
Type 3 is a limited token with administrative privileges removed and administrative groups disabled.  The limited token is used when User Account Control is enabled, the application does not require administrative privilege, and the User does not choose to start the program using Run as administrator.

LogName=Security
SourceName= Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4624
EventType=0
Type=Information
ComputerName=ops-sys-002
TaskCategory=Logon
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=162902394
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=An account was successfully logged on.

Subject:
 Security ID:  Domain_B\SYSTEM
 Account Name:  ops-sys-002
 Account Domain:  Domain_B
 Logon ID:  0x70E4

Logon Information:
 Logon Type:  3
 Restricted Admin Mode: Yes
 Virtual Account:  No
 Elevated Token:  No

Impersonation Level:  Identification

New Logon:
 Security ID:  Domain_B\user_a
 Account Name:  user_a
 Account Domain:  Domain_B
 Logon ID:  0x6C10
 Linked Logon ID:  C40B
 Network Account Name: user_c
 Network Account Domain: Domain_E
 Logon GUID:  {27C4A2F2-13CA-AA25-E903-D31268740239}

Process Information:
 Process ID:  0x1456
 Process Name:  C:\Windows\System32\example_a.exe

Network Information:
 Workstation Name: ops-sys-002
 Source Network Address: -
 Source Port:  46255

Detailed Authentication Information:
 Logon Process:  Winlogon 
 Authentication Package: Negotiate
 Transited Services: service_A
 Package Name (NTLM only): -
 Key Length:  0

This event is generated when a logon session is created. It is generated on the computer that was accessed.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as 12F0E.exe or 12F0E.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

01/28/2020 01:20:47 PM
LogName=Security
SourceName=Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4688
EventType=0
Type=Information
ComputerName=$SPLUNK_HOME/etc/apps/Splunk_TA_windows/samples/hostname.sample
TaskCategory=Process Creation
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=714270325
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=A new process has been created.
Subject:
	Security ID:		Domain_D\user_h
	Account Name:		user_h
	Account Domain:		Domain_D
	Logon ID:		0xA19C
Process Information:
	New Process ID:		0x2A35
	New Process Name:	C:\Windows\System32\example_a.exe
	Token Elevation Type:	TokenElevationTypeFull (2)
	Creator Process ID:	0xC7A0
Token Elevation Type indicates the type of token that was assigned to the new process in accordance with User Account Control policy.
Type 1 is a full token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  A full token is only used if User Account Control is disabled or if the User is the built-in Administrator account or a service account.
Type 2 is an elevated token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  An elevated token is used when User Account Control is enabled and the User chooses to start the program using Run as administrator.  An elevated token is also used when an application is configured to always require administrative privilege or to always require maximum privilege, and the User is a member of the Administrators group.
Type 3 is a limited token with administrative privileges removed and administrative groups disabled.  The limited token is used when User Account Control is enabled, the application does not require administrative privilege, and the User does not choose to start the program using Run as administrator.

LogName=Security
SourceName=Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4688
EventType=0
Type=Information
ComputerName=$SPLUNK_HOME/etc/apps/Splunk_TA_windows/samples/hostname.sample
TaskCategory=Process Creation
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=461114548
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=A new process has been created.
Subject:
	Security ID:		Domain_E\user_j
	Account Name:		user_j
	Account Domain:		Domain_E
	Logon ID:		0xB111
Process Information:
	New Process ID:		0x0FA4
	New Process Name:	C:\Windows\System32\example_c.exe
	Token Elevation Type:	TokenElevationTypeLimited (3)
	Creator Process ID:	0xFA96
Token Elevation Type indicates the type of token that was assigned to the new process in accordance with User Account Control policy.
Type 1 is a full token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  A full token is only used if User Account Control is disabled or if the User is the built-in Administrator account or a service account.
Type 2 is an elevated token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  An elevated token is used when User Account Control is enabled and the User chooses to start the program using Run as administrator.  An elevated token is also used when an application is configured to always require administrative privilege or to always require maximum privilege, and the User is a member of the Administrators group.
Type 3 is a limited token with administrative privileges removed and administrative groups disabled.  The limited token is used when User Account Control is enabled, the application does not require administrative privilege, and the User does not choose to start the program using Run as administrator.

LogName=Security
SourceName= Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4624
EventType=0
Type=Information
ComputerName=ACME-005
TaskCategory=Logon
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=833469251
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=An account was successfully logged on.

Subject:
 Security ID:  Domain_D\SYSTEM
 Account Name:  ACME-005
 Account Domain:  Domain_D
 Logon ID:  0x70E4

Logon Information:
 Logon Type:  7
 Restricted Admin Mode: Yes
 Virtual Account:  No
 Elevated Token:  No

Impersonation Level:  Identification

New Logon:
 Security ID:  Domain_D\user_d
 Account Name:  user_d
 Account Domain:  Domain_D
 Logon ID:  0x3EC3
 Linked Logon ID:  94A3
 Network Account Name: user_f
 Network Account Domain: Domain_A
 Logon GUID:  {0887F1E4-39EA-D53C-804F-31D568A06274}

Process Information:
 Process ID:  0xC4ED
 Process Name:  C:\Windows\System32\example_b.exe

Network Information:
 Workstation Name: ACME-005
 Source Network Address: -
 Source Port:  43297

Detailed Authentication Information:
 Logon Process:  Winlogon 
 Authentication Package: Negotiate
 Transited Services: service_D
 Package Name (NTLM only): -
 Key Length:  0

This event is generated when a logon session is created. It is generated on the computer that was accessed.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as 3CC1E.exe or 3CC1E.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

01/28/2020 01:20:39 PM
LogName=Security
SourceName= Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4624
EventType=0
Type=Information
ComputerName=HOST-005
TaskCategory=Logon
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=558836208
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=An account was successfully logged on.

Subject:
 Security ID:  Domain_A\SYSTEM
 Account Name:  HOST-005
 Account Domain:  Domain_A
 Logon ID:  0x70E4

Logon Information:
 Logon Type:  7
 Restricted Admin Mode: Yes
 Virtual Account:  No
 Elevated Token:  Yes

Impersonation Level:  Delegation

New Logon:
 Security ID:  Domain_A\user_j
 Account Name:  user_j
 Account Domain:  Domain_A
 Logon ID:  0xB111
 Linked Logon ID:  DB3E
 Network Account Name: -
 Network Account Domain: -
 Logon GUID:  {0887F1E4-39EA-D53C-804F-31D568A06274}

Process Information:
 Process ID:  0xE4C9
 Process Name:  C:\Windows\System32\example_f.exe

Network Information:
 Workstation Name: HOST-005
 Source Network Address: 241.25.246.91
 Source Port:  41178

Detailed Authentication Information:
 Logon Process:  Winlogon 
 Authentication Package: Negotiate
 Transited Services: service_D
 Package Name (NTLM only): -
 Key Length:  0

This event is generated when a logon session is created. It is generated on the computer that was accessed.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as 5B7AE.exe or 5B7AE.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

LogName=Security
SourceName=Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4688
EventType=0
Type=Information
ComputerName=$SPLUNK_HOME/etc/apps/Splunk_TA_windows/samples/hostname.sample
TaskCategory=Process Creation
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=603472874
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=A new process has been created.
Subject:
	Security ID:		Domain_E\user_l
	Account Name:		user_l
	Account Domain:		Domain_E
	Logon ID:		0xAB37
Process Information:
	New Process ID:		0x8E8B
	New Process Name:	C:\Windows\System32\example_a.exe
	Token Elevation Type:	TokenElevationTypeDefault (1)
	Creator Process ID:	0x5155
Token Elevation Type indicates the type of token that was assigned to the new process in accordance with User Account Control policy.
Type 1 is a full token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  A full token is only used if User Account Control is disabled or if the User is the built-in Administrator account or a service account.
Type 2 is an elevated token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  An elevated token is used when User Account Control is enabled and the User chooses to start the program using Run as administrator.  An elevated token is also used when an application is configured to always require administrative privilege or to always require maximum privilege, and the User is a member of the Administrators group.
Type 3 is a limited token with administrative privileges removed and administrative groups disabled.  The limited token is used when User Account Control is enabled, the application does not require administrative privilege, and the User does not choose to start the program using Run as administrator.

LogName=Security
SourceName=Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4688
EventType=0
Type=Information
ComputerName=$SPLUNK_HOME/etc/apps/Splunk_TA_windows/samples/hostname.sample
TaskCategory=Process Creation
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=192362994
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=A new process has been created.
Subject:
	Security ID:		Domain_B\user_m
	Account Name:		user_m
	Account Domain:		Domain_B
	Logon ID:		0x46BA
Process Information:
	New Process ID:		0x3EAD
	New Process Name:	C:\Windows\System32\example_f.exe
	Token Elevation Type:	TokenElevationTypeDefault (1)
	Creator Process ID:	0x8EFC
Token Elevation Type indicates the type of token that was assigned to the new process in accordance with User Account Control policy.
Type 1 is a full token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  A full token is only used if User Account Control is disabled or if the User is the built-in Administrator account or a service account.
Type 2 is an elevated token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  An elevated token is used when User Account Control is enabled and the User chooses to start the program using Run as administrator.  An elevated token is also used when an application is configured to always require administrative privilege or to always require maximum privilege, and the User is a member of the Administrators group.
Type 3 is a limited token with administrative privileges removed and administrative groups disabled.  The limited token is used when User Account Control is enabled, the application does not require administrative privilege, and the User does not choose to start the program using Run as administrator.

01/28/2020 01:20:28 PM
LogName=Security
SourceName=Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4625
EventType=Information
Type=Information
ComputerName=BUSDEV-008
TaskCategory=Authentication Policy Change
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=475220821
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=An account failed to log on.

Subject:
	Security ID:		NT AUTHORITY\SYSTEM
	Account Name:		ADMINISTRATOR
	Account Domain:		WIN81$
	Logon ID:		0xD

Logon Type:		15

Account For Which Logon Failed:
	Security ID:		NT AUTHORITY\SYSTEM
	Account Name:		ADMINISTRATOR
	Account Domain:		WIN81$

Failure Information:
	Failure Reason:		Unknown User name or bad password.
	Status:			0xAE2D521B
	Sub Status:		0xAE2D521B

Process Information:
	Caller Process ID:	0xD
	Caller Process Name:	-

Network Information:
	Workstation Name:	-
	Source Network Address:	210.241.15.243
	Source Port:		40830

Detailed Authentication Information:
	Logon Process:		AE2D521B 
	Authentication Package:	NTLM
	Transited Services:	-
	Package Name (NTLM only):	-
	Key Length:		15

This event is generated when a logon request fails. It is generated on the computer where access was attempted.

The Subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as 7E6ADBA.exe or 7E6ADBA.exe.

The Logon Type field indicates the kind of logon that was requested. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The Process Information fields indicate which account and process on the system requested the logon.

The Network Information fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
	- Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
	- Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
	- Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

LogName=Security
SourceName= Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4624
EventType=0
Type=Information
ComputerName=ops-sys-003
TaskCategory=Logon
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=136731324
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=An account was successfully logged on.

Subject:
 Security ID:  Domain_C\SYSTEM
 Account Name:  ops-sys-003
 Account Domain:  Domain_C
 Logon ID:  0x70E4

Logon Information:
 Logon Type:  3
 Restricted Admin Mode: -
 Virtual Account:  No
 Elevated Token:  No

Impersonation Level:  Impersonation

New Logon:
 Security ID:  Domain_C\user_k
 Account Name:  user_k
 Account Domain:  Domain_C
 Logon ID:  0xBAC3
 Linked Logon ID:  9ABD
 Network Account Name: -
 Network Account Domain: Domain_E
 Logon GUID:  {00000000-0000-0000-0000-000000000000}

Process Information:
 Process ID:  0x7920
 Process Name:  C:\Windows\System32\example_c.exe

Network Information:
 Workstation Name: ops-sys-003
 Source Network Address: -
 Source Port:  63388

Detailed Authentication Information:
 Logon Process:  Winlogon 
 Authentication Package: Kerberos
 Transited Services: service_B
 Package Name (NTLM only): -
 Key Length:  0

This event is generated when a logon session is created. It is generated on the computer that was accessed.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as 5591B.exe or 5591B.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

Keywords=Audit Success
Message=A new process has been created.
Subject:
	Security ID:		Domain_D\user_c
	Account Name:		user_c
	Account Domain:		Domain_D
	Logon ID:		0x5FC9
Process Information:
	New Process ID:		0x840F
	New Process Name:	C:\Windows\System32\example_e.exe
	Token Elevation Type:	TokenElevationTypeFull (2)
	Creator Process ID:	0x0C84
Token Elevation Type indicates the type of token that was assigned to the new process in accordance with User Account Control policy.
Type 1 is a full token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  A full token is only used if User Account Control is disabled or if the User is the built-in Administrator account or a service account.
Type 2 is an elevated token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  An elevated token is used when User Account Control is enabled and the User chooses to start the program using Run as administrator.  An elevated token is also used when an application is configured to always require administrative privilege or to always require maximum privilege, and the User is a member of the Administrators group.
Type 3 is a limited token with administrative privileges removed and administrative groups disabled.  The limited token is used when User Account Control is enabled, the application does not require administrative privilege, and the User does not choose to start the program using Run as administrator.

LogName=Security
SourceName= Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4624
EventType=0
Type=Information
ComputerName=PROD-POS-001
TaskCategory=Logon
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=716759213
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=An account was successfully logged on.

Subject:
 Security ID:  Domain_D\SYSTEM
 Account Name:  PROD-POS-001
 Account Domain:  Domain_D
 Logon ID:  0x70E4

Logon Information:
 Logon Type:  9
 Restricted Admin Mode: No
 Virtual Account:  No
 Elevated Token:  No

Impersonation Level:  Delegation

New Logon:
 Security ID:  Domain_D\user_l
 Account Name:  user_l
 Account Domain:  Domain_D
 Logon ID:  0xAB37
 Linked Logon ID:  19B6
 Network Account Name: user_l
 Network Account Domain: -
 Logon GUID:  {00000000-0000-0000-0000-000000000000}

Process Information:
 Process ID:  0xE7F7
 Process Name:  C:\Windows\System32\example_f.exe

Network Information:
 Workstation Name: PROD-POS-001
 Source Network Address: 172.37.27.87
 Source Port:  8192

Detailed Authentication Information:
 Logon Process:  Winlogon 
 Authentication Package: Kerberos
 Transited Services: service_B
 Package Name (NTLM only): -
 Key Length:  0

This event is generated when a logon session is created. It is generated on the computer that was accessed.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as 8264A.exe or 8264A.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

01/28/2020 01:20:22 PM
LogName=Security
SourceName=Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4688
EventType=0
Type=Information
ComputerName=$SPLUNK_HOME/etc/apps/Splunk_TA_windows/samples/hostname.sample
TaskCategory=Process Creation
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=751816672
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=A new process has been created.
Subject:
	Security ID:		Domain_A\user_f
	Account Name:		user_f
	Account Domain:		Domain_A
	Logon ID:		0xA369
Process Information:
	New Process ID:		0x79AD
	New Process Name:	C:\Windows\System32\example_b.exe
	Token Elevation Type:	TokenElevationTypeDefault (1)
	Creator Process ID:	0x90F7
Token Elevation Type indicates the type of token that was assigned to the new process in accordance with User Account Control policy.
Type 1 is a full token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  A full token is only used if User Account Control is disabled or if the User is the built-in Administrator account or a service account.
Type 2 is an elevated token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  An elevated token is used when User Account Control is enabled and the User chooses to start the program using Run as administrator.  An elevated token is also used when an application is configured to always require administrative privilege or to always require maximum privilege, and the User is a member of the Administrators group.
Type 3 is a limited token with administrative privileges removed and administrative groups disabled.  The limited token is used when User Account Control is enabled, the application does not require administrative privilege, and the User does not choose to start the program using Run as administrator.

LogName=Security
SourceName=Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4625
EventType=Information
Type=Information
ComputerName=BUSDEV-002
TaskCategory=Authentication Policy Change
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=397204333
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=An account failed to log on.

Subject:
	Security ID:		abc\def
	Account Name:		ABCDE
	Account Domain:		WIN81$
	Logon ID:		0xD

Logon Type:		2

Account For Which Logon Failed:
	Security ID:		abc\def
	Account Name:		ABCDE
	Account Domain:		WIN81$

Failure Information:
	Failure Reason:		Unknown User name or bad password.
	Status:			0xA4E87933
	Sub Status:		0xA4E87933

Process Information:
	Caller Process ID:	0xD
	Caller Process Name:	-

Network Information:
	Workstation Name:	-
	Source Network Address:	253.120.142.110
	Source Port:		45773

Detailed Authentication Information:
	Logon Process:		A4E87933 
	Authentication Package:	NTLM
	Transited Services:	-
	Package Name (NTLM only):	-
	Key Length:		2

This event is generated when a logon request fails. It is generated on the computer where access was attempted.

The Subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as 7FA71FD.exe or 7FA71FD.exe.

The Logon Type field indicates the kind of logon that was requested. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The Process Information fields indicate which account and process on the system requested the logon.

The Network Information fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
	- Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
	- Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
	- Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

LogName=Security
SourceName= Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4624
EventType=0
Type=Information
ComputerName=PROD-MFS-001
TaskCategory=Logon
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=830171850
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=An account was successfully logged on.

Subject:
 Security ID:  Domain_A\SYSTEM
 Account Name:  PROD-MFS-001
 Account Domain:  Domain_A
 Logon ID:  0x70E4

Logon Information:
 Logon Type:  4
 Restricted Admin Mode: -
 Virtual Account:  No
 Elevated Token:  Yes

Impersonation Level:  Delegation

New Logon:
 Security ID:  Domain_A\user_k
 Account Name:  user_k
 Account Domain:  Domain_A
 Logon ID:  0xBAC3
 Linked Logon ID:  484F
 Network Account Name: user_f
 Network Account Domain: -
 Logon GUID:  {27C4A2F2-13CA-AA25-E903-D31268740239}

Process Information:
 Process ID:  0xF668
 Process Name:  C:\Windows\System32\example_a.exe

Network Information:
 Workstation Name: PROD-MFS-001
 Source Network Address: 24.147.63.69
 Source Port:  62553

Detailed Authentication Information:
 Logon Process:  logonProcess1 
 Authentication Package: Kerberos
 Transited Services: service_B
 Package Name (NTLM only): -
 Key Length:  0

This event is generated when a logon session is created. It is generated on the computer that was accessed.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as A1276.exe or A1276.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

EventType=Information
Type=Information
ComputerName=PROD-POS-004
TaskCategory=Authentication Policy Change
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=445234141
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=An account was successfully logged on.

Subject:
	Security ID:		NT AUTHORITY\SYSTEM
	Account Name:		ADMINISTRATOR
	Account Domain:		abc
	Logon ID:		0x8FC
Logon Information:
	Logon Type:		7
	Restricted Admin Mode:	-
	Virtual Account:		Yes
	Elevated Token:		Yes

Impersonation Level:		Impersonation

New Logon:
	Security ID:		NT AUTHORITY\SYSTEM
	Account Name:		ADMINISTRATOR
	Account Domain:		abc
	Logon ID:		0x8FC	Linked Logon ID:		0xC
	Network Account Name:	-
	Network Account Domain:	-
	Logon GUID:		{A71FC744-9BD0-9BD0-9BD0-0AB27FA88B06}

Process Information:
	Process ID:		0x8FC	Process Name:		win\directory\directory2\55771C0.exe

Network Information:
	Workstation Name:	-
	Source Network Address:	-
	Source Port:		1788

Detailed Authentication Information:
	Logon Process:		A71FC744  
	Authentication Package:	NTLM
	Transited Services:	-
	Package Name (NTLM only):	-
	Key Length:		7

This event is generated when a logon session is created. It is generated on the computer that was accessed.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as 55771C0.exe or 55771C0.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
	- Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
	- Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
	- Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
	- Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

LogName=Security
SourceName=Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4688
EventType=0
Type=Information
ComputerName=$SPLUNK_HOME/etc/apps/Splunk_TA_windows/samples/hostname.sample
TaskCategory=Process Creation
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=692921044
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=A new process has been created.
Subject:
	Security ID:		Domain_B\user_f
	Account Name:		user_f
	Account Domain:		Domain_B
	Logon ID:		0xA369
Process Information:
	New Process ID:		0x3342
	New Process Name:	C:\Windows\System32\example_e.exe
	Token Elevation Type:	TokenElevationTypeDefault (1)
	Creator Process ID:	0x2EC2
Token Elevation Type indicates the type of token that was assigned to the new process in accordance with User Account Control policy.
Type 1 is a full token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  A full token is only used if User Account Control is disabled or if the User is the built-in Administrator account or a service account.
Type 2 is an elevated token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  An elevated token is used when User Account Control is enabled and the User chooses to start the program using Run as administrator.  An elevated token is also used when an application is configured to always require administrative privilege or to always require maximum privilege, and the User is a member of the Administrators group.
Type 3 is a limited token with administrative privileges removed and administrative groups disabled.  The limited token is used when User Account Control is enabled, the application does not require administrative privilege, and the User does not choose to start the program using Run as administrator.

LogName=Security
SourceName=Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4688
EventType=0
Type=Information
ComputerName=$SPLUNK_HOME/etc/apps/Splunk_TA_windows/samples/hostname.sample
TaskCategory=Process Creation
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=381005368
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=A new process has been created.
Subject:
	Security ID:		Domain_B\user_h
	Account Name:		user_h
	Account Domain:		Domain_B
	Logon ID:		0xA19C
Process Information:
	New Process ID:		0xF952
	New Process Name:	C:\Windows\System32\example_b.exe
	Token Elevation Type:	TokenElevationTypeFull (2)
	Creator Process ID:	0x22E4
Token Elevation Type indicates the type of token that was assigned to the new process in accordance with User Account Control policy.
Type 1 is a full token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  A full token is only used if User Account Control is disabled or if the User is the built-in Administrator account or a service account.
Type 2 is an elevated token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  An elevated token is used when User Account Control is enabled and the User chooses to start the program using Run as administrator.  An elevated token is also used when an application is configured to always require administrative privilege or to always require maximum privilege, and the User is a member of the Administrators group.
Type 3 is a limited token with administrative privileges removed and administrative groups disabled.  The limited token is used when User Account Control is enabled, the application does not require administrative privilege, and the User does not choose to start the program using Run as administrator.

LogName=Security
SourceName= Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4624
EventType=0
Type=Information
ComputerName=ops-sys-001
TaskCategory=Logon
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=495152100
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=An account was successfully logged on.

Subject:
 Security ID:  Domain_C\SYSTEM
 Account Name:  ops-sys-001
 Account Domain:  Domain_C
 Logon ID:  0x70E4

Logon Information:
 Logon Type:  5
 Restricted Admin Mode: Yes
 Virtual Account:  No
 Elevated Token:  No

Impersonation Level:  Delegation

New Logon:
 Security ID:  Domain_C\user_n
 Account Name:  user_n
 Account Domain:  Domain_C
 Logon ID:  0x4D76
 Linked Logon ID:  DD7C
 Network Account Name: -
 Network Account Domain: -
 Logon GUID:  {00000000-0000-0000-0000-000000000000}

Process Information:
 Process ID:  0x56EE
 Process Name:  C:\Windows\System32\example_a.exe

Network Information:
 Workstation Name: ops-sys-001
 Source Network Address: 64.255.187.229
 Source Port:  31692

Detailed Authentication Information:
 Logon Process:  Winlogon 
 Authentication Package: Kerberos
 Transited Services: service_B
 Package Name (NTLM only): -
 Key Length:  0

This event is generated when a logon session is created. It is generated on the computer that was accessed.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as 3D95B.exe or 3D95B.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

01/28/2020 01:20:11 PM
LogName=Security
SourceName=Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4688
EventType=0
Type=Information
ComputerName=$SPLUNK_HOME/etc/apps/Splunk_TA_windows/samples/hostname.sample
TaskCategory=Process Creation
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=399538223
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=A new process has been created.
Subject:
	Security ID:		Domain_A\user_a
	Account Name:		user_a
	Account Domain:		Domain_A
	Logon ID:		0x6C10
Process Information:
	New Process ID:		0x821D
	New Process Name:	C:\Windows\System32\example_f.exe
	Token Elevation Type:	TokenElevationTypeDefault (1)
	Creator Process ID:	0xF11B
Token Elevation Type indicates the type of token that was assigned to the new process in accordance with User Account Control policy.
Type 1 is a full token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  A full token is only used if User Account Control is disabled or if the User is the built-in Administrator account or a service account.
Type 2 is an elevated token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  An elevated token is used when User Account Control is enabled and the User chooses to start the program using Run as administrator.  An elevated token is also used when an application is configured to always require administrative privilege or to always require maximum privilege, and the User is a member of the Administrators group.
Type 3 is a limited token with administrative privileges removed and administrative groups disabled.  The limited token is used when User Account Control is enabled, the application does not require administrative privilege, and the User does not choose to start the program using Run as administrator.

LogName=Security
SourceName= Microsoft Windows security auditing.

Subject:
 Security ID:  Domain_D\SYSTEM
 Account Name:  BUSDEV-005
 Account Domain:  Domain_D
 Logon ID:  0x70E4

Logon Information:
 Logon Type:  11
 Restricted Admin Mode: Yes
 Virtual Account:  No
 Elevated Token:  Yes

Impersonation Level:  Identification

New Logon:
 Security ID:  Domain_D\user_i
 Account Name:  user_i
 Account Domain:  Domain_D
 Logon ID:  0x5F25
 Linked Logon ID:  CA1C
 Network Account Name: -
 Network Account Domain: Domain_C
 Logon GUID:  {0887F1E4-39EA-D53C-804F-31D568A06274}

Process Information:
 Process ID:  0xA1BB
 Process Name:  C:\Windows\System32\example_e.exe

Network Information:
 Workstation Name: BUSDEV-005
 Source Network Address: 105.202.206.131
 Source Port:  31809

Detailed Authentication Information:
 Logon Process:  Winlogon 
 Authentication Package: Kerberos
 Transited Services: service_D
 Package Name (NTLM only): -
 Key Length:  0

This event is generated when a logon session is created. It is generated on the computer that was accessed.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as C76AC.exe or C76AC.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

LogName=Security
SourceName=Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4688
EventType=0
Type=Information
ComputerName=$SPLUNK_HOME/etc/apps/Splunk_TA_windows/samples/hostname.sample
TaskCategory=Process Creation
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=283771155
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=A new process has been created.
Subject:
	Security ID:		Domain_A\user_k
	Account Name:		user_k
	Account Domain:		Domain_A
	Logon ID:		0xBAC3
Process Information:
	New Process ID:		0xD288
	New Process Name:	C:\Windows\System32\example_d.exe
	Token Elevation Type:	TokenElevationTypeDefault (1)
	Creator Process ID:	0x08F4
Token Elevation Type indicates the type of token that was assigned to the new process in accordance with User Account Control policy.
Type 1 is a full token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  A full token is only used if User Account Control is disabled or if the User is the built-in Administrator account or a service account.
Type 2 is an elevated token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  An elevated token is used when User Account Control is enabled and the User chooses to start the program using Run as administrator.  An elevated token is also used when an application is configured to always require administrative privilege or to always require maximum privilege, and the User is a member of the Administrators group.
Type 3 is a limited token with administrative privileges removed and administrative groups disabled.  The limited token is used when User Account Control is enabled, the application does not require administrative privilege, and the User does not choose to start the program using Run as administrator.

01/28/2020 01:20:04 PM
LogName=Security
SourceName=Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4688
EventType=0
Type=Information
ComputerName=$SPLUNK_HOME/etc/apps/Splunk_TA_windows/samples/hostname.sample
TaskCategory=Process Creation
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=745811958
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=A new process has been created.
Subject:
	Security ID:		Domain_B\user_n
	Account Name:		user_n
	Account Domain:		Domain_B
	Logon ID:		0x4D76
Process Information:
	New Process ID:		0x8FF8
	New Process Name:	C:\Windows\System32\example_e.exe
	Token Elevation Type:	TokenElevationTypeLimited (3)
	Creator Process ID:	0x97D9
Token Elevation Type indicates the type of token that was assigned to the new process in accordance with User Account Control policy.
Type 1 is a full token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  A full token is only used if User Account Control is disabled or if the User is the built-in Administrator account or a service account.
Type 2 is an elevated token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  An elevated token is used when User Account Control is enabled and the User chooses to start the program using Run as administrator.  An elevated token is also used when an application is configured to always require administrative privilege or to always require maximum privilege, and the User is a member of the Administrators group.
Type 3 is a limited token with administrative privileges removed and administrative groups disabled.  The limited token is used when User Account Control is enabled, the application does not require administrative privilege, and the User does not choose to start the program using Run as administrator.

LogName=Security
SourceName= Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4624
EventType=0
Type=Information
ComputerName=BUSDEV-001
TaskCategory=Logon
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=180116265
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=An account was successfully logged on.

Subject:
 Security ID:  Domain_D\SYSTEM
 Account Name:  BUSDEV-001
 Account Domain:  Domain_D
 Logon ID:  0x70E4

Logon Information:
 Logon Type:  7
 Restricted Admin Mode: Yes
 Virtual Account:  No
 Elevated Token:  No

Impersonation Level:  Impersonation

New Logon:
 Security ID:  Domain_D\user_n
 Account Name:  user_n
 Account Domain:  Domain_D
 Logon ID:  0x4D76
 Linked Logon ID:  1704
 Network Account Name: -
 Network Account Domain: Domain_E
 Logon GUID:  {27C4A2F2-13CA-AA25-E903-D31268740239}

Process Information:
 Process ID:  0x9F38
 Process Name:  C:\Windows\System32\example_a.exe

Network Information:
 Workstation Name: BUSDEV-001
 Source Network Address: -
 Source Port:  49443

Detailed Authentication Information:
 Logon Process:  User32 
 Authentication Package: Negotiate
 Transited Services: service_B
 Package Name (NTLM only): -
 Key Length:  0

This event is generated when a logon session is created. It is generated on the computer that was accessed.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as 53F35.exe or 53F35.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

This event is generated when a logon request fails. It is generated on the computer where access was attempted.

The Subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as 76FA62C.exe or 76FA62C.exe.

The Logon Type field indicates the kind of logon that was requested. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The Process Information fields indicate which account and process on the system requested the logon.

The Network Information fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
	- Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
	- Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
	- Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

LogName=Security
SourceName=Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4688
EventType=0
Type=Information
ComputerName=$SPLUNK_HOME/etc/apps/Splunk_TA_windows/samples/hostname.sample
TaskCategory=Process Creation
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=184531614
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=A new process has been created.
Subject:
	Security ID:		Domain_C\user_h
	Account Name:		user_h
	Account Domain:		Domain_C
	Logon ID:		0xA19C
Process Information:
	New Process ID:		0xEBBD
	New Process Name:	C:\Windows\System32\example_f.exe
	Token Elevation Type:	TokenElevationTypeFull (2)
	Creator Process ID:	0xF9FC
Token Elevation Type indicates the type of token that was assigned to the new process in accordance with User Account Control policy.
Type 1 is a full token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  A full token is only used if User Account Control is disabled or if the User is the built-in Administrator account or a service account.
Type 2 is an elevated token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  An elevated token is used when User Account Control is enabled and the User chooses to start the program using Run as administrator.  An elevated token is also used when an application is configured to always require administrative privilege or to always require maximum privilege, and the User is a member of the Administrators group.
Type 3 is a limited token with administrative privileges removed and administrative groups disabled.  The limited token is used when User Account Control is enabled, the application does not require administrative privilege, and the User does not choose to start the program using Run as administrator.

	Security ID:		NT AUTHORITY\SYSTEM
	Account Name:		ADMINISTRATOR
	Account Domain:		Backup Operators
	Logon ID:		0xA

Logon Type:		19

Account For Which Logon Failed:
	Security ID:		NT AUTHORITY\SYSTEM
	Account Name:		ADMINISTRATOR
	Account Domain:		Backup Operators

Failure Information:
	Failure Reason:		Unknown User name or bad password.
	Status:			0xB35C77D3
	Sub Status:		0xB35C77D3

Process Information:
	Caller Process ID:	0xA
	Caller Process Name:	-

Network Information:
	Workstation Name:	-
	Source Network Address:	241.77.76.134
	Source Port:		50786

Detailed Authentication Information:
	Logon Process:		B35C77D3 
	Authentication Package:	NTLM
	Transited Services:	-
	Package Name (NTLM only):	-
	Key Length:		19

This event is generated when a logon request fails. It is generated on the computer where access was attempted.

The Subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as CB1B6D5.exe or CB1B6D5.exe.

The Logon Type field indicates the kind of logon that was requested. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The Process Information fields indicate which account and process on the system requested the logon.

The Network Information fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
	- Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
	- Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
	- Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

This event is generated when a logon session is created. It is generated on the computer that was accessed.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as 6E488.exe or 6E488.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.
