LogName=Security
SourceName=Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4688
EventType=0
Type=Information
ComputerName=$SPLUNK_HOME/etc/apps/Splunk_TA_windows/samples/hostname.sample
TaskCategory=Process Creation
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=727362307
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=A new process has been created.
Subject:
	Security ID:		Domain_E\user_i
	Account Name:		user_i
	Account Domain:		Domain_E
	Logon ID:		0x5F25
Process Information:
	New Process ID:		0xB173
	New Process Name:	C:\Windows\System32\example_c.exe
	Token Elevation Type:	TokenElevationTypeLimited (3)
	Creator Process ID:	0x74F9
Token Elevation Type indicates the type of token that was assigned to the new process in accordance with User Account Control policy.
Type 1 is a full token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  A full token is only used if User Account Control is disabled or if the User is the built-in Administrator account or a service account.
Type 2 is an elevated token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  An elevated token is used when User Account Control is enabled and the User chooses to start the program using Run as administrator.  An elevated token is also used when an application is configured to always require administrative privilege or to always require maximum privilege, and the User is a member of the Administrators group.
Type 3 is a limited token with administrative privileges removed and administrative groups disabled.  The limited token is used when User Account Control is enabled, the application does not require administrative privilege, and the User does not choose to start the program using Run as administrator.

LogName=Security
SourceName= Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4624
EventType=0
Type=Information
ComputerName=SE-003
TaskCategory=Logon
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=954006465
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=An account was successfully logged on.

Subject:
 Security ID:  Domain_B\SYSTEM
 Account Name:  SE-003
 Account Domain:  Domain_B
 Logon ID:  0x70E4

Logon Information:
 Logon Type:  6
 Restricted Admin Mode: No
 Virtual Account:  No
 Elevated Token:  Yes

Impersonation Level:  Delegation

New Logon:
 Security ID:  Domain_B\user_n
 Account Name:  user_n
 Account Domain:  Domain_B
 Logon ID:  0x4D76
 Linked Logon ID:  4FA6
 Network Account Name: -
 Network Account Domain: -
 Logon GUID:  {27C4A2F2-13CA-AA25-E903-D31268740239}

Process Information:
 Process ID:  0x748D
 Process Name:  C:\Windows\System32\example_e.exe

Network Information:
 Workstation Name: SE-003
 Source Network Address: 200.159.75.150
 Source Port:  37511

Detailed Authentication Information:
 Logon Process:  User32 
 Authentication Package: Kerberos
 Transited Services: -
 Package Name (NTLM only): -
 Key Length:  0

This event is generated when a logon session is created. It is generated on the computer that was accessed.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as A7E72.exe or A7E72.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

LogName=Security
SourceName=Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4688
EventType=0
Type=Information
ComputerName=$SPLUNK_HOME/etc/apps/Splunk_TA_windows/samples/hostname.sample
TaskCategory=Process Creation
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=184912602
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=A new process has been created.
Subject:
	Security ID:		Domain_C\user_l
	Account Name:		user_l
	Account Domain:		Domain_C
	Logon ID:		0xAB37
Process Information:
	New Process ID:		0x76BF
	New Process Name:	C:\Windows\System32\example_c.exe
	Token Elevation Type:	TokenElevationTypeLimited (3)
	Creator Process ID:	0xA645
Token Elevation Type indicates the type of token that was assigned to the new process in accordance with User Account Control policy.
Type 1 is a full token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  A full token is only used if User Account Control is disabled or if the User is the built-in Administrator account or a service account.
Type 2 is an elevated token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  An elevated token is used when User Account Control is enabled and the User chooses to start the program using Run as administrator.  An elevated token is also used when an application is configured to always require administrative privilege or to always require maximum privilege, and the User is a member of the Administrators group.
Type 3 is a limited token with administrative privileges removed and administrative groups disabled.  The limited token is used when User Account Control is enabled, the application does not require administrative privilege, and the User does not choose to start the program using Run as administrator.

LogName=Security
SourceName= Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4624
EventType=0
Type=Information
ComputerName=ops-sys-002
TaskCategory=Logon
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=780110409
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=An account was successfully logged on.

Subject:
 Security ID:  Domain_B\SYSTEM
 Account Name:  ops-sys-002
 Account Domain:  Domain_B
 Logon ID:  0x70E4

Logon Information:
 Logon Type:  9
 Restricted Admin Mode: Yes
 Virtual Account:  No
 Elevated Token:  No

Impersonation Level:  Identification

New Logon:
 Security ID:  Domain_B\user_k
 Account Name:  user_k
 Account Domain:  Domain_B
 Logon ID:  0xBAC3
 Linked Logon ID:  86C5
 Network Account Name: -
 Network Account Domain: Domain_B
 Logon GUID:  {00000000-0000-0000-0000-000000000000}

Process Information:
 Process ID:  0x2A03
 Process Name:  C:\Windows\System32\example_a.exe

Network Information:
 Workstation Name: ops-sys-002
 Source Network Address: 87.233.112.217
 Source Port:  63126

Detailed Authentication Information:
 Logon Process:  Winlogon 
 Authentication Package: Negotiate
 Transited Services: -
 Package Name (NTLM only): -
 Key Length:  0

This event is generated when a logon session is created. It is generated on the computer that was accessed.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as C859E.exe or C859E.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

An elevated token is used when User Account Control is enabled and the User chooses to start the program using Run as administrator.  An elevated token is also used when an application is configured to always require administrative privilege or to always require maximum privilege, and the User is a member of the Administrators group.
Type 3 is a limited token with administrative privileges removed and administrative groups disabled.  The limited token is used when User Account Control is enabled, the application does not require administrative privilege, and the User does not choose to start the program using Run as administrator.

 Restricted Admin Mode: -
 Virtual Account:  No
 Elevated Token:  Yes

Impersonation Level:  Impersonation

New Logon:
 Security ID:  Domain_D\user_f
 Account Name:  user_f
 Account Domain:  Domain_D
 Logon ID:  0xA369
 Linked Logon ID:  FDFD
 Network Account Name: -
 Network Account Domain: -
 Logon GUID:  {0887F1E4-39EA-D53C-804F-31D568A06274}

Process Information:
 Process ID:  0x018E
 Process Name:  C:\Windows\System32\example_c.exe

Network Information:
 Workstation Name: ACME-001
 Source Network Address: 172.87.183.93
 Source Port:  25512

Detailed Authentication Information:
 Logon Process:  logonProcess1 
 Authentication Package: Kerberos
 Transited Services: -
 Package Name (NTLM only): -
 Key Length:  0

This event is generated when a logon session is created. It is generated on the computer that was accessed.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as 4C0A9.exe or 4C0A9.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

LogName=Security
SourceName=Microsoft Windows security auditing.

Type=Information
ComputerName=$SPLUNK_HOME/etc/apps/Splunk_TA_windows/samples/hostname.sample
TaskCategory=Process Creation
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=963989021
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=A new process has been created.
Subject:
	Security ID:		Domain_E\user_l
	Account Name:		user_l
	Account Domain:		Domain_E
	Logon ID:		0xAB37
Process Information:
	New Process ID:		0xF8C8
	New Process Name:	C:\Windows\System32\example_e.exe
	Token Elevation Type:	TokenElevationTypeDefault (1)
	Creator Process ID:	0xF5CC
Token Elevation Type indicates the type of token that was assigned to the new process in accordance with User Account Control policy.
Type 1 is a full token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  A full token is only used if User Account Control is disabled or if the User is the built-in Administrator account or a service account.
Type 2 is an elevated token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  An elevated token is used when User Account Control is enabled and the User chooses to start the program using Run as administrator.  An elevated token is also used when an application is configured to always require administrative privilege or to always require maximum privilege, and the User is a member of the Administrators group.
Type 3 is a limited token with administrative privileges removed and administrative groups disabled.  The limited token is used when User Account Control is enabled, the application does not require administrative privilege, and the User does not choose to start the program using Run as administrator.

LogName=Security
SourceName= Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4624
EventType=0
Type=Information
ComputerName=BUSDEV-005
TaskCategory=Logon
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=974487317
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=An account was successfully logged on.

Subject:
 Security ID:  Domain_D\SYSTEM
 Account Name:  BUSDEV-005
 Account Domain:  Domain_D
 Logon ID:  0x70E4

Logon Information:
 Logon Type:  3
 Restricted Admin Mode: No
 Virtual Account:  No
 Elevated Token:  Yes

Impersonation Level:  Identification

New Logon:
 Security ID:  Domain_D\user_l
 Account Name:  user_l
 Account Domain:  Domain_D
 Logon ID:  0xAB37
 Linked Logon ID:  3E4A
 Network Account Name: -
 Network Account Domain: -
 Logon GUID:  {0887F1E4-39EA-D53C-804F-31D568A06274}

Process Information:
 Process ID:  0xE86D
 Process Name:  C:\Windows\System32\example_e.exe

Network Information:
 Workstation Name: BUSDEV-005
 Source Network Address: 118.173.172.76
 Source Port:  20012

Detailed Authentication Information:
 Logon Process:  logonProcess1 
 Authentication Package: Kerberos
 Transited Services: -
 Package Name (NTLM only): -
 Key Length:  0

This event is generated when a logon session is created. It is generated on the computer that was accessed.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as 14080.exe or 14080.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

This event is generated when a logon session is created. It is generated on the computer that was accessed.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as 3F998.exe or 3F998.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

This event is generated when a logon request fails. It is generated on the computer where access was attempted.

The Subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as E4425A8.exe or E4425A8.exe.

The Logon Type field indicates the kind of logon that was requested. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The Process Information fields indicate which account and process on the system requested the logon.

The Network Information fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
	- Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
	- Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
	- Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

LogName=Security
SourceName=Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4688
EventType=0
Type=Information
ComputerName=$SPLUNK_HOME/etc/apps/Splunk_TA_windows/samples/hostname.sample
TaskCategory=Process Creation
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=796462053
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=A new process has been created.
Subject:
	Security ID:		Domain_A\user_j
	Account Name:		user_j
	Account Domain:		Domain_A
	Logon ID:		0xB111
Process Information:
	New Process ID:		0xFF6A
	New Process Name:	C:\Windows\System32\example_c.exe
	Token Elevation Type:	TokenElevationTypeFull (2)
	Creator Process ID:	0x22B8
Token Elevation Type indicates the type of token that was assigned to the new process in accordance with User Account Control policy.
Type 1 is a full token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  A full token is only used if User Account Control is disabled or if the User is the built-in Administrator account or a service account.
Type 2 is an elevated token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  An elevated token is used when User Account Control is enabled and the User chooses to start the program using Run as administrator.  An elevated token is also used when an application is configured to always require administrative privilege or to always require maximum privilege, and the User is a member of the Administrators group.
Type 3 is a limited token with administrative privileges removed and administrative groups disabled.  The limited token is used when User Account Control is enabled, the application does not require administrative privilege, and the User does not choose to start the program using Run as administrator.

LogName=Security
SourceName= Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4624
EventType=0
Type=Information
ComputerName=HOST-005
TaskCategory=Logon
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=255708383
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=An account was successfully logged on.

Subject:
 Security ID:  Domain_B\SYSTEM
 Account Name:  HOST-005
 Account Domain:  Domain_B
 Logon ID:  0x70E4

Logon Information:
 Logon Type:  8
 Restricted Admin Mode: No
 Virtual Account:  No
 Elevated Token:  No

Impersonation Level:  Delegation

New Logon:
 Security ID:  Domain_B\user_k
 Account Name:  user_k
 Account Domain:  Domain_B
 Logon ID:  0xBAC3
 Linked Logon ID:  A7C7
 Network Account Name: user_n
 Network Account Domain: -
 Logon GUID:  {221B21A6-1AE2-3F9A-24EF-22C392AC2A47}

Process Information:
 Process ID:  0x5BDA
 Process Name:  C:\Windows\System32\example_d.exe

Network Information:
 Workstation Name: HOST-005
 Source Network Address: -
 Source Port:  32142

Detailed Authentication Information:
 Logon Process:  Winlogon 
 Authentication Package: Kerberos
 Transited Services: service_A
 Package Name (NTLM only): -
 Key Length:  0

This event is generated when a logon session is created. It is generated on the computer that was accessed.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as ADA17.exe or ADA17.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

This event is generated when a process attempts to log on an account by explicitly specifying that account's credentials. This most commonly occurs in batch-type configurations such as scheduled tasks, or when using the RUNAS command.

 Logon ID:  0x70E4

Logon Information:
 Logon Type:  9
 Restricted Admin Mode: -
 Virtual Account:  Yes
 Elevated Token:  No

Impersonation Level:  Impersonation

New Logon:
 Security ID:  Domain_A\user_i
 Account Name:  user_i
 Account Domain:  Domain_A
 Logon ID:  0x5F25
 Linked Logon ID:  290B
 Network Account Name: -
 Network Account Domain: Domain_A
 Logon GUID:  {221B21A6-1AE2-3F9A-24EF-22C392AC2A47}

Process Information:
 Process ID:  0x2BAE
 Process Name:  C:\Windows\System32\example_c.exe

Network Information:
 Workstation Name: COREDEV-002
 Source Network Address: 25.105.228.72
 Source Port:  42445

Detailed Authentication Information:
 Logon Process:  logonProcess1 
 Authentication Package: Negotiate
 Transited Services: service_D
 Package Name (NTLM only): -
 Key Length:  0

This event is generated when a logon session is created. It is generated on the computer that was accessed.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as 71C35.exe or 71C35.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

LogName=Security
SourceName=Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4688
EventType=0
Type=Information
ComputerName=$SPLUNK_HOME/etc/apps/Splunk_TA_windows/samples/hostname.sample
TaskCategory=Process Creation
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=807038310
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=A new process has been created.
Subject:
	Security ID:		Domain_B\user_e
	Account Name:		user_e
	Account Domain:		Domain_B
	Logon ID:		0x0452
Process Information:
	New Process ID:		0x63C6
	New Process Name:	C:\Windows\System32\example_b.exe
	Token Elevation Type:	TokenElevationTypeFull (2)
	Creator Process ID:	0xB243
Token Elevation Type indicates the type of token that was assigned to the new process in accordance with User Account Control policy.
Type 1 is a full token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  A full token is only used if User Account Control is disabled or if the User is the built-in Administrator account or a service account.
Type 2 is an elevated token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  An elevated token is used when User Account Control is enabled and the User chooses to start the program using Run as administrator.  An elevated token is also used when an application is configured to always require administrative privilege or to always require maximum privilege, and the User is a member of the Administrators group.
Type 3 is a limited token with administrative privileges removed and administrative groups disabled.  The limited token is used when User Account Control is enabled, the application does not require administrative privilege, and the User does not choose to start the program using Run as administrator.

LogName=Security
SourceName=Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4625
EventType=Information
Type=Information
ComputerName=COREDEV-005
TaskCategory=Authentication Policy Change
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=576161132
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=An account failed to log on.

Subject:
	Security ID:		WINDOWS\SERVER2012$
	Account Name:		ADMINISTRATOR
	Account Domain:		krbtgt
	Logon ID:		0x0

Logon Type:		15

Account For Which Logon Failed:
	Security ID:		WINDOWS\SERVER2012$
	Account Name:		ADMINISTRATOR
	Account Domain:		krbtgt

Failure Information:
	Failure Reason:		Unknown User name or bad password.
	Status:			0x67B5A666
	Sub Status:		0x67B5A666

Process Information:
	Caller Process ID:	0x0
	Caller Process Name:	-

Network Information:
	Workstation Name:	-
	Source Network Address:	146.43.80.189
	Source Port:		48653

Detailed Authentication Information:
	Logon Process:		67B5A666 
	Authentication Package:	Negotiate
	Transited Services:	-
	Package Name (NTLM only):	-
	Key Length:		15

This event is generated when a logon request fails. It is generated on the computer where access was attempted.

The Subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as 43D4A67.exe or 43D4A67.exe.

The Logon Type field indicates the kind of logon that was requested. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The Process Information fields indicate which account and process on the system requested the logon.

The Network Information fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
	- Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
	- Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
	- Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

01/28/2020 01:19:33 PM
LogName=Security
SourceName=Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4688
EventType=0
Type=Information
ComputerName=$SPLUNK_HOME/etc/apps/Splunk_TA_windows/samples/hostname.sample
TaskCategory=Process Creation
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=411947772
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=A new process has been created.
Subject:
	Security ID:		Domain_E\user_a
	Account Name:		user_a
	Account Domain:		Domain_E
	Logon ID:		0x6C10
Process Information:
	New Process ID:		0x4A4A
	New Process Name:	C:\Windows\System32\example_b.exe
	Token Elevation Type:	TokenElevationTypeDefault (1)
	Creator Process ID:	0xEBCB
Token Elevation Type indicates the type of token that was assigned to the new process in accordance with User Account Control policy.
Type 1 is a full token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  A full token is only used if User Account Control is disabled or if the User is the built-in Administrator account or a service account.
Type 2 is an elevated token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  An elevated token is used when User Account Control is enabled and the User chooses to start the program using Run as administrator.  An elevated token is also used when an application is configured to always require administrative privilege or to always require maximum privilege, and the User is a member of the Administrators group.
Type 3 is a limited token with administrative privileges removed and administrative groups disabled.  The limited token is used when User Account Control is enabled, the application does not require administrative privilege, and the User does not choose to start the program using Run as administrator.

Impersonation Level:  Impersonation

 Security ID:  Domain_B\user_n
 Account Name:  user_n
 Account Domain:  Domain_B
 Logon ID:  0x4D76
 Linked Logon ID:  1662
 Network Account Name: -
 Network Account Domain: -
 Logon GUID:  {0887F1E4-39EA-D53C-804F-31D568A06274}

Process Information:
 Process ID:  0xB86F
 Process Name:  C:\Windows\System32\example_e.exe

Network Information:
 Workstation Name: COREDEV-001
 Source Network Address: 78.181.120.174
 Source Port:  47808

Detailed Authentication Information:
 Logon Process:  Winlogon 
 Authentication Package: Negotiate
 Transited Services: service_B
 Package Name (NTLM only): -
 Key Length:  0

This event is generated when a logon session is created. It is generated on the computer that was accessed.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as 8EADE.exe or 8EADE.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

TaskCategory=Process Creation
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=553281516
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=A new process has been created.
Subject:
	Security ID:		Domain_B\user_f
	Account Name:		user_f
	Account Domain:		Domain_B
	Logon ID:		0xA369
Process Information:
	New Process ID:		0xB4E7
	New Process Name:	C:\Windows\System32\example_c.exe
	Token Elevation Type:	TokenElevationTypeFull (2)
	Creator Process ID:	0xA976
Token Elevation Type indicates the type of token that was assigned to the new process in accordance with User Account Control policy.
Type 1 is a full token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  A full token is only used if User Account Control is disabled or if the User is the built-in Administrator account or a service account.
Type 2 is an elevated token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  An elevated token is used when User Account Control is enabled and the User chooses to start the program using Run as administrator.  An elevated token is also used when an application is configured to always require administrative privilege or to always require maximum privilege, and the User is a member of the Administrators group.
Type 3 is a limited token with administrative privileges removed and administrative groups disabled.  The limited token is used when User Account Control is enabled, the application does not require administrative privilege, and the User does not choose to start the program using Run as administrator.

LogName=Security
SourceName=Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4624
EventType=Information
Type=Information
ComputerName=HOST-006
TaskCategory=Authentication Policy Change
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=809049946
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=An account was successfully logged on.

Subject:
	Security ID:		WINDOWS\ADSERVER
	Account Name:		ADMINISTRATOR
	Account Domain:		TASERVER$
	Logon ID:		0x350
Logon Information:
	Logon Type:		15
	Restricted Admin Mode:	-
	Virtual Account:		Yes
	Elevated Token:		Yes

Impersonation Level:		Abcde

New Logon:
	Security ID:		WINDOWS\ADSERVER
	Account Name:		ADMINISTRATOR
	Account Domain:		TASERVER$
	Logon ID:		0x350	Linked Logon ID:		0xA
	Network Account Name:	-
	Network Account Domain:	-
	Logon GUID:		{C1B26134-BA1B-BA1B-BA1B-6CB7D9ADE5FD}

Process Information:
	Process ID:		0x350	Process Name:		win\directory\directory2\B7C3937.exe

Network Information:
	Workstation Name:	-
	Source Network Address:	-
	Source Port:		2906

Detailed Authentication Information:
	Logon Process:		C1B26134  
	Authentication Package:	NTLM
	Transited Services:	-
	Package Name (NTLM only):	-
	Key Length:		15

This event is generated when a logon session is created. It is generated on the computer that was accessed.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as B7C3937.exe or B7C3937.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
	- Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
	- Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
	- Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
	- Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

Type 1 is a full token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  A full token is only used if User Account Control is disabled or if the User is the built-in Administrator account or a service account.
Type 2 is an elevated token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  An elevated token is used when User Account Control is enabled and the User chooses to start the program using Run as administrator.  An elevated token is also used when an application is configured to always require administrative privilege or to always require maximum privilege, and the User is a member of the Administrators group.
Type 3 is a limited token with administrative privileges removed and administrative groups disabled.  The limited token is used when User Account Control is enabled, the application does not require administrative privilege, and the User does not choose to start the program using Run as administrator.

01/28/2020 01:19:27 PM
LogName=Security
SourceName= Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4624
EventType=0
Type=Information
ComputerName=ops-sys-004
TaskCategory=Logon
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=105023330
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=An account was successfully logged on.

Subject:
 Security ID:  Domain_B\SYSTEM
 Account Name:  ops-sys-004
 Account Domain:  Domain_B
 Logon ID:  0x70E4

Logon Information:
 Logon Type:  8
 Restricted Admin Mode: Yes
 Virtual Account:  Yes
 Elevated Token:  Yes

Impersonation Level:  Identification

New Logon:
 Security ID:  Domain_B\user_g
 Account Name:  user_g
 Account Domain:  Domain_B
 Logon ID:  0xEB5F
 Linked Logon ID:  8A23
 Network Account Name: user_j
 Network Account Domain: -
 Logon GUID:  {27C4A2F2-13CA-AA25-E903-D31268740239}

Process Information:
 Process ID:  0x0A8B
 Process Name:  C:\Windows\System32\example_c.exe

Network Information:
 Workstation Name: ops-sys-004
 Source Network Address: -
 Source Port:  42152

Detailed Authentication Information:
 Logon Process:  User32 
 Authentication Package: Kerberos
 Transited Services: service_A
 Package Name (NTLM only): -
 Key Length:  0

This event is generated when a logon session is created. It is generated on the computer that was accessed.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as 90AB6.exe or 90AB6.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

01/28/2020 01:19:24 PM
LogName=Security
SourceName=Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4688
EventType=0
Type=Information
ComputerName=$SPLUNK_HOME/etc/apps/Splunk_TA_windows/samples/hostname.sample
TaskCategory=Process Creation
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=953035380
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=A new process has been created.
Subject:
	Security ID:		Domain_C\user_j
	Account Name:		user_j
	Account Domain:		Domain_C
	Logon ID:		0xB111
Process Information:
	New Process ID:		0x5EC2
	New Process Name:	C:\Windows\System32\example_e.exe
	Token Elevation Type:	TokenElevationTypeDefault (1)
	Creator Process ID:	0xA1F1
Token Elevation Type indicates the type of token that was assigned to the new process in accordance with User Account Control policy.
Type 1 is a full token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  A full token is only used if User Account Control is disabled or if the User is the built-in Administrator account or a service account.
Type 2 is an elevated token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  An elevated token is used when User Account Control is enabled and the User chooses to start the program using Run as administrator.  An elevated token is also used when an application is configured to always require administrative privilege or to always require maximum privilege, and the User is a member of the Administrators group.
Type 3 is a limited token with administrative privileges removed and administrative groups disabled.  The limited token is used when User Account Control is enabled, the application does not require administrative privilege, and the User does not choose to start the program using Run as administrator.

LogName=Security
SourceName=Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4688
EventType=0
Type=Information
ComputerName=$SPLUNK_HOME/etc/apps/Splunk_TA_windows/samples/hostname.sample
TaskCategory=Process Creation
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=399328890
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=A new process has been created.
Subject:
	Security ID:		Domain_C\user_i
	Account Name:		user_i
	Account Domain:		Domain_C
	Logon ID:		0x5F25
Process Information:
	New Process ID:		0x1EE9
	New Process Name:	C:\Windows\System32\example_g.exe
	Token Elevation Type:	TokenElevationTypeDefault (1)
	Creator Process ID:	0x8B34
Token Elevation Type indicates the type of token that was assigned to the new process in accordance with User Account Control policy.
Type 1 is a full token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  A full token is only used if User Account Control is disabled or if the User is the built-in Administrator account or a service account.
Type 2 is an elevated token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  An elevated token is used when User Account Control is enabled and the User chooses to start the program using Run as administrator.  An elevated token is also used when an application is configured to always require administrative privilege or to always require maximum privilege, and the User is a member of the Administrators group.
Type 3 is a limited token with administrative privileges removed and administrative groups disabled.  The limited token is used when User Account Control is enabled, the application does not require administrative privilege, and the User does not choose to start the program using Run as administrator.

 Security ID:  Domain_A\SYSTEM
 Account Name:  HOST-005
 Account Domain:  Domain_A
 Logon ID:  0x70E4

Logon Information:
 Logon Type:  5
 Restricted Admin Mode: Yes
 Virtual Account:  Yes
 Elevated Token:  No

Impersonation Level:  Delegation

New Logon:
 Security ID:  Domain_A\user_b
 Account Name:  user_b
 Account Domain:  Domain_A
 Logon ID:  0x3A81
 Linked Logon ID:  B885
 Network Account Name: user_f
 Network Account Domain: Domain_A
 Logon GUID:  {0887F1E4-39EA-D53C-804F-31D568A06274}

Process Information:
 Process ID:  0x52A6
 Process Name:  C:\Windows\System32\example_g.exe

Network Information:
 Workstation Name: HOST-005
 Source Network Address: 114.112.36.82
 Source Port:  5295

Detailed Authentication Information:
 Logon Process:  User32 
 Authentication Package: Negotiate
 Transited Services: service_D
 Package Name (NTLM only): -
 Key Length:  0

This event is generated when a logon session is created. It is generated on the computer that was accessed.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as 3B409.exe or 3B409.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

TaskCategory=Process Creation
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=456727230
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=A new process has been created.
Subject:
	Security ID:		Domain_C\user_e
	Account Name:		user_e
	Account Domain:		Domain_C
	Logon ID:		0x0452
Process Information:
	New Process ID:		0xC616
	New Process Name:	C:\Windows\System32\example_f.exe
	Token Elevation Type:	TokenElevationTypeFull (2)
	Creator Process ID:	0xCAE2
Token Elevation Type indicates the type of token that was assigned to the new process in accordance with User Account Control policy.
Type 1 is a full token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  A full token is only used if User Account Control is disabled or if the User is the built-in Administrator account or a service account.
Type 2 is an elevated token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  An elevated token is used when User Account Control is enabled and the User chooses to start the program using Run as administrator.  An elevated token is also used when an application is configured to always require administrative privilege or to always require maximum privilege, and the User is a member of the Administrators group.
Type 3 is a limited token with administrative privileges removed and administrative groups disabled.  The limited token is used when User Account Control is enabled, the application does not require administrative privilege, and the User does not choose to start the program using Run as administrator.

01/28/2020 01:19:16 PM
LogName=Security
SourceName= Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4624
EventType=0
Type=Information
ComputerName=COREDEV-001
TaskCategory=Logon
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=754732704
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=An account was successfully logged on.

Subject:
 Security ID:  Domain_B\SYSTEM
 Account Name:  COREDEV-001
 Account Domain:  Domain_B
 Logon ID:  0x70E4

Logon Information:
 Logon Type:  10
 Restricted Admin Mode: Yes
 Virtual Account:  No
 Elevated Token:  No

Impersonation Level:  Delegation

New Logon:
 Security ID:  Domain_B\user_a
 Account Name:  user_a
 Account Domain:  Domain_B
 Logon ID:  0x6C10
 Linked Logon ID:  87AE
 Network Account Name: user_i
 Network Account Domain: Domain_E
 Logon GUID:  {221B21A6-1AE2-3F9A-24EF-22C392AC2A47}

Process Information:
 Process ID:  0x2A18
 Process Name:  C:\Windows\System32\example_c.exe

Network Information:
 Workstation Name: COREDEV-001
 Source Network Address: 32.19.159.241
 Source Port:  6388

Detailed Authentication Information:
 Logon Process:  User32 
 Authentication Package: Kerberos
 Transited Services: service_D
 Package Name (NTLM only): -
 Key Length:  0

This event is generated when a logon session is created. It is generated on the computer that was accessed.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as 8A44D.exe or 8A44D.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

01/28/2020 01:19:15 PM
LogName=Security
SourceName=Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4688
EventType=0
Type=Information
ComputerName=$SPLUNK_HOME/etc/apps/Splunk_TA_windows/samples/hostname.sample
TaskCategory=Process Creation
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=519234535
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=A new process has been created.
Subject:
	Security ID:		Domain_E\user_g
	Account Name:		user_g
	Account Domain:		Domain_E
	Logon ID:		0xEB5F
Process Information:
	New Process ID:		0x6946
	New Process Name:	C:\Windows\System32\example_d.exe
	Token Elevation Type:	TokenElevationTypeDefault (1)
	Creator Process ID:	0x777E
Token Elevation Type indicates the type of token that was assigned to the new process in accordance with User Account Control policy.
Type 1 is a full token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  A full token is only used if User Account Control is disabled or if the User is the built-in Administrator account or a service account.
Type 2 is an elevated token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  An elevated token is used when User Account Control is enabled and the User chooses to start the program using Run as administrator.  An elevated token is also used when an application is configured to always require administrative privilege or to always require maximum privilege, and the User is a member of the Administrators group.
Type 3 is a limited token with administrative privileges removed and administrative groups disabled.  The limited token is used when User Account Control is enabled, the application does not require administrative privilege, and the User does not choose to start the program using Run as administrator.

01/28/2020 01:19:13 PM
LogName=Security
SourceName= Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4624
EventType=0
Type=Information
ComputerName=BUSDEV-001
TaskCategory=Logon
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=821340703
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=An account was successfully logged on.

Subject:
 Security ID:  Domain_B\SYSTEM
 Account Name:  BUSDEV-001
 Account Domain:  Domain_B
 Logon ID:  0x70E4

Logon Information:
 Logon Type:  10
 Restricted Admin Mode: Yes
 Virtual Account:  No
 Elevated Token:  Yes

Impersonation Level:  Impersonation

New Logon:
 Security ID:  Domain_B\user_g
 Account Name:  user_g
 Account Domain:  Domain_B
 Logon ID:  0xEB5F
 Linked Logon ID:  C91F
 Network Account Name: -
 Network Account Domain: Domain_B
 Logon GUID:  {27C4A2F2-13CA-AA25-E903-D31268740239}

Process Information:
 Process ID:  0x6E5C
 Process Name:  C:\Windows\System32\example_e.exe

Network Information:
 Workstation Name: BUSDEV-001
 Source Network Address: -
 Source Port:  56724

Detailed Authentication Information:
 Logon Process:  User32 
 Authentication Package: Kerberos
 Transited Services: service_D
 Package Name (NTLM only): -
 Key Length:  0

This event is generated when a logon session is created. It is generated on the computer that was accessed.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as 5D3A8.exe or 5D3A8.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

 Package Name (NTLM only): -
 Key Length:  0

This event is generated when a logon session is created. It is generated on the computer that was accessed.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as 33FA2.exe or 33FA2.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

LogName=Security
SourceName=Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4688
EventType=0
Type=Information
ComputerName=$SPLUNK_HOME/etc/apps/Splunk_TA_windows/samples/hostname.sample
TaskCategory=Process Creation
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=362136783
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=A new process has been created.
Subject:
	Security ID:		Domain_C\user_h
	Account Name:		user_h
	Account Domain:		Domain_C
	Logon ID:		0xA19C
Process Information:
	New Process ID:		0x049C
	New Process Name:	C:\Windows\System32\example_f.exe
	Token Elevation Type:	TokenElevationTypeDefault (1)
	Creator Process ID:	0x16E2
Token Elevation Type indicates the type of token that was assigned to the new process in accordance with User Account Control policy.
Type 1 is a full token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  A full token is only used if User Account Control is disabled or if the User is the built-in Administrator account or a service account.
Type 2 is an elevated token with no privileges removed or groups disabled.  An elevated token is used when User Account Control is enabled and the User chooses to start the program using Run as administrator.  An elevated token is also used when an application is configured to always require administrative privilege or to always require maximum privilege, and the User is a member of the Administrators group.
Type 3 is a limited token with administrative privileges removed and administrative groups disabled.  The limited token is used when User Account Control is enabled, the application does not require administrative privilege, and the User does not choose to start the program using Run as administrator.
